\\n20: Use the new OpenFeature-based feature flag client for all new feature flags. There are some differences compared to the legacy `config.featureToggles` system:\\n21: \\n22: - Feature flag initialisation is async, but will be finished by the time the UI is rendered. This means you cannot get the value of a feature flag at the 'top level' of a module/file\\n23: - Call `evaluateBooleanFlag(\\\"flagName\\\")` from `@grafana/runtime/internal` instead to get the value of a feature flag\\n24: - Feature flag values _may_ change over the lifetime of the session. \\n20: Use the new OpenFeature-based feature flag client for all new feature flags. There are some differences compared to the legacy `config.featureToggles` system:\\n21: \\n22: - Feature flag initialisation is async, but will be finished by the time the UI is rendered. This means you cannot get the value of a feature flag at the 'top level' of a module/file\\n23: - Call `evaluateBooleanFlag(\\\"flagName\\\")` from `@grafana/runtime/internal` instead to get the value of a feature flag\\n24: - Feature flag values _may_ change over the lifetime of the session. Do not store the value in a variable that is used for longer than a single render - always call `evaluateBooleanFlag` lazily when you use the value.\\n25: \\n26: \",\"endLine\":26,\"startLine\":19},{\"content\":\"11: \\n12: Once your feature toggle is defined, you can then wrap your feature around a check if the feature flag is enabled on that Grafana instance.\\n13: \\n14: \",\"endLine\":14,\"startLine\":11},{\"content\":\"1: # Feature toggle guide\\n2: \\n3: This guide helps you to add your feature behind a _feature flag_, code that lets you enable or disable a feature without redeploying Grafana.\\n4: \\n5: ## Steps to adding a feature toggle\\n6: \\n7: 1. \n20: Use the new OpenFeature-based feature flag client for all new feature flags. There are some differences compared to the legacy `config.featureToggles` system:\n21: \n22: - Feature flag initialisation is async, but will be finished by the time the UI is rendered. This means you cannot get the value of a feature flag at the 'top level' of a module/file\n23: - Call `evaluateBooleanFlag(\"flagName\")` from `@grafana/runtime/internal` instead to get the value of a feature flag\n24: - Feature flag values _may_ change over the lifetime of the session. Do not store the value in a variable that is used for longer than a single render - always call `evaluateBooleanFlag` lazily when you use the value.\n25: \n26: ","endLine":26,"startLine":19},{"content":"11: \n12: Once your feature toggle is defined, you can then wrap your feature around a check if the feature flag is enabled on that Grafana instance.\n13: \n14: ","endLine":14,"startLine":11},{"content":"1: # Feature toggle guide\n2: \n3: This guide helps you to add your feature behind a _feature flag_, code that lets you enable or disable a feature without redeploying Grafana.\n4: \n5: ## Steps to adding a feature toggle\n6: \n7: 1. `pkg/services/ssosettings/ssosettingsimpl/service.go`: Main `Service` implementation with `ProvideService()` function that creates the service, registers API endpoints, and sets up providers (OAuth, LDAP, SAML)\\n- `pkg/services/ssosettings/strategies/`: Strategy pattern implementations for different SSO providers:\\n  - `oauth_strategy.go`: OAuth provider configuration\\n  - `ldap_strategy.go`: Wiring**\\n- `pkg/services/ssosettings/api/api.go`: REST API endpoints (`ProvideApi()` function, `RegisterAPIEndpoints()` method) registering GET/PUT/DELETE operations on `/api/v1/sso-settings` with access control middleware using `ActionSettingsRead`, `ActionSettingsWrite`, and `ScopeSettingsOAuth(key)`\\n- `pkg/login/social/socialimpl/service.go`: `SocialService` with `ProvideService()` function that loads SSO settings at startup and creates OAuth connectors for each provider\\n- `pkg/services/authn/authn.go`: `SSOSettingsAwareClient` interface that OAuth clients implement to provide SSO configuration\\n- `pkg/services/authn/clients/oauth.go`: OAuth authentication client (`ProvideOAuth()` function) implementing `SSOSettingsAwareClient` to get configuration from SSO settings\\n- `ssosettingsimpl.ProvideService()` call and DI wiring\\n\\n**Integration Points**\\n- `pkg/services/ldap/service/ldap.go`: LDAP service registers as a Reloadable with SSO settings when `FlagSsoSettingsLDAP` is enabled\\n- `pkg/services/navtree/navtreeimpl/admin.go`: Admin UI navigation uses `OauthSettingsEvaluator` and `EvalAuthenticationSettings` for menu visibility\\n- `pkg/api/api.go`: Main API sets up admin auth page evaluator using both evaluators\\n- `pkg/services/pluginsintegration/pluginsso/pluginsso.go`: Plugin integration accesses SSO settings via `DefaultSettingsProvider`\\n\\nThe architecture implements a clean separation where the feature flag enables the new SSO Settings API system, the service layer manages settings lifecycle, the API layer exposes REST endpoints with proper access control, and the authentication clients consume settings to configure OAuth, LDAP, and SAML
